			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">

				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div role="note" class="hatnote">"IPCC" redirects here. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/IPCC_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="IPCC (disambiguation)">IPCC (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<p>The <b>Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change</b> (<b>IPCC</b>) is a scientific and <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_organization" title="Intergovernmental organization">intergovernmental body</a> under the auspices of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> set up at the request of member governments, dedicated to the task of providing the world with an objective, scientific view of <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a> and its political and economic impacts.<sup id="cite_ref-Weart_international_80s_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weart_international_80s-3">[3]</a></sup> It was first established in 1988 by two United Nations organizations, the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a> (WMO) and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Environment_Programme" title="United Nations Environment Programme">United Nations Environment Programme</a> (UNEP), and later endorsed by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a> through Resolution 43/53. Membership of the IPCC is open to all members of the WMO and UNEP.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> The IPCC produces reports that support the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Framework_Convention_on_Climate_Change" title="United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change">United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change</a> (UNFCCC), which is the main international treaty on climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-unfccc_intro_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unfccc_intro-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-principles_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-principles-6">[6]</a></sup> The ultimate objective of the UNFCCC is to "stabilize greenhouse gas concentrations in the atmosphere at a level that would prevent dangerous anthropogenic [i.e., human-induced] interference with the climate system".<sup id="cite_ref-unfccc_intro_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unfccc_intro-5">[5]</a></sup> IPCC reports cover "the scientific, technical and socio-economic information relevant to understanding the scientific basis of risk of human-induced climate change, <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming" title="Effects of global warming">its potential impacts</a> and options for <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_adaptation" title="Climate change adaptation">adaptation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_mitigation" title="Climate change mitigation">mitigation</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-principles_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-principles-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>The IPCC does not carry out its own original research, nor does it do the work of monitoring climate or related phenomena itself. The IPCC <a href="/wiki/Systematic_review" title="Systematic review">bases its assessment on the published literature</a>, which includes <a href="/wiki/Peer-review" class="mw-redirect" title="Peer-review">peer-reviewed</a> and non-peer-reviewed sources.<sup id="cite_ref-iac_sources_for_ipcc_report_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iac_sources_for_ipcc_report-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Thousands of scientists and other experts contribute (on a voluntary basis, without payment from the IPCC)<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> to writing and reviewing reports, which are then reviewed by governments. IPCC reports contain a "<a href="/wiki/Summary_for_Policymakers" class="mw-redirect" title="Summary for Policymakers">Summary for Policymakers</a>", which is subject to line-by-line approval by delegates from all participating governments. Typically this involves the governments of more than 120 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-understanding_ipcc_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-understanding_ipcc-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>The IPCC provides an internationally accepted authority on climate change,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> producing reports which have the agreement of leading climate scientists and the consensus of participating governments. The <a href="/wiki/2007_Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="2007 Nobel Peace Prize">2007</a> <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> was shared, in equal parts, between the IPCC and <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins_and_aims">Origins and aims</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Origins and aims">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The IPCC developed from an international scientific body, the <a href="/wiki/Advisory_Group_on_Greenhouse_Gases" title="Advisory Group on Greenhouse Gases">Advisory Group on Greenhouse Gases</a> set up in 1985 by the <a href="/wiki/International_Council_for_Science" title="International Council for Science">International Council of Scientific Unions</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Environment_Programme" title="United Nations Environment Programme">United Nations Environment Programme</a> (UNEP), and the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a> (WMO) to provide recommendations based on current research. This small group of scientists lacked the resources to cover the increasingly complex interdisciplinary nature of climate science, The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">United States Environmental Protection Agency</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_State_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="United States State Department">State Department</a> wanted an international convention to agree restrictions on <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gases</a>, and the conservative <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Ronald_Reagan" title="Presidency of Ronald Reagan">Reagan Administration</a> was concerned about unrestrained influence from independent scientists or from United Nations bodies including UNEP and the WMO. The U.S. government was the main force in forming the IPCC as an autonomous intergovernmental body in which scientists took part both as experts on the science and as official representatives of their governments, to produce reports which had the firm backing of all the leading scientists worldwide researching the topic, and which then had to gain consensus agreement from every one of the participating governments. In this way, it was formed as a hybrid between a scientific body and an intergovernmental political organisation.<sup id="cite_ref-Weart_international_80s_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weart_international_80s-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>The principles that the IPCC operates under<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-12">[12]</a></sup> are set out in the relevant WMO Executive Council and UNEP Governing Council resolutions and decisions, as well as on actions in support of the UNFCCC process.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>The aims of the IPCC are to assess scientific information relevant to:<sup id="cite_ref-principles_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-principles-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<ol>
<li>Human-induced climate change,</li>
<li>The impacts of human-induced climate change,</li>
<li>Options for adaptation and mitigation.</li>
</ol>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization">Organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Korean economist <a href="/wiki/Hoesung_Lee" title="Hoesung Lee">Hoesung Lee</a> is the chair of the IPCC since October 8, 2015, following the election of the new IPCC Bureau.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Before this election, the IPCC was led by his vice-Chair <a href="/wiki/Ismail_El_Gizouli" title="Ismail El Gizouli">Ismail El Gizouli</a>, who was designated acting Chair after the resignation of <a href="/wiki/Rajendra_K._Pachauri" title="Rajendra K. Pachauri">Rajendra K. Pachauri</a> in February 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The previous chairs were <a href="/wiki/Rajendra_K._Pachauri" title="Rajendra K. Pachauri">Rajendra K. Pachauri</a>, elected in May 2002; <a href="/wiki/Robert_Watson_(scientist)" title="Robert Watson (scientist)">Robert Watson</a> in 1997; and <a href="/wiki/Bert_Bolin" title="Bert Bolin">Bert Bolin</a> in 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The chair is assisted by an elected bureau including vice-chairs, working group co-chairs, and a secretariat.</p>
<p>The IPCC Panel is composed of representatives appointed by governments and organizations. Participation of delegates with appropriate expertise is encouraged. Plenary sessions of the IPCC and IPCC <a href="/wiki/Working_group" title="Working group">Working groups</a> are held at the level of government representatives. Non Governmental and Intergovernmental Organizations may be allowed to attend as observers. Sessions of the IPCC Bureau, workshops, expert and lead authors meetings are by invitation only.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Attendance at the 2003 meeting included 350 government officials and climate change experts. After the opening ceremonies, closed plenary sessions were held.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The meeting report<sup id="cite_ref-ipcc2006_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipcc2006-19">[19]</a></sup> states there were 322 persons in attendance at Sessions with about seven-eighths of participants being from governmental organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-ipcc2006_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipcc2006-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are several major groups:</p>
<ul>
<li>IPCC Panel: Meets in plenary session about once a year and controls the organization's structure, procedures, and work program. The Panel is the IPCC corporate entity.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-20">[20]</a></sup></li>
<li>Chair: Elected by the Panel.</li>
<li>Secretariat: Oversees and manages all activities. Supported by UNEP and WMO.</li>
<li>Bureau: Elected by the Panel. Chaired by the Chair. 30 members include IPCC Vice-Chairs, Co-Chairs and Vice-Chairs of Working Groups and Task Force.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></li>
<li>Working Groups: Each has two Co-Chairs, one from the developed and one from developing world, and a technical support unit.
<ul>
<li>Working Group I: Assesses scientific aspects of the climate system and climate change. Co-Chairs: Valérie Masson-Delmotte and Panmao Zhai<sup id="cite_ref-ipcc2015election_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipcc2015election-22">[22]</a></sup></li>
<li>Working Group II: Assesses vulnerability of socio-economic and natural systems to climate change, consequences, and adaptation options. Co-Chairs: Hans-Otto Pörtner and Debra Roberts<sup id="cite_ref-ipcc2015election_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipcc2015election-22">[22]</a></sup></li>
<li>Working Group III: Assesses options for limiting greenhouse gas emissions and otherwise mitigating climate change. Co-Chairs: Priyadarshi R. Shukla and <a href="/wiki/James_Skea" title="James Skea">Jim Skea</a><sup id="cite_ref-ipcc2015election_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipcc2015election-22">[22]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Task Force on National Greenhouse Gas Inventories<sup id="cite_ref-:0_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-20">[20]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>The IPCC receives funding through the IPCC Trust Fund, established in 1989 by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Environment_Programme" title="United Nations Environment Programme">United Nations Environment Programme</a> (UNEP) and the <a href="/wiki/World_Meteorological_Organization" title="World Meteorological Organization">World Meteorological Organization</a> (WMO), Costs of the Secretary and of housing the secretariat are provided by the WMO, while UNEP meets the cost of the Depute Secretary. Annual cash contributions to the Trust Fund are made by the WMO, by UNEP, and by IPCC Members; the scale of payments is determined by the IPCC Panel, which is also responsible for considering and adopting by consensus the annual budget. The organisation is required to comply with the Financial Regulations and Rules of the WMO.<sup id="cite_ref-IPCC_funding_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPCC_funding-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Assessment_reports">Assessment reports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Assessment reports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="toccolours" style="float: right; border-sollapse: collapse; margin: 0 0 1.5em 1.5em;" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="2">

<p>The IPCC has published five comprehensive assessment reports reviewing the latest climate science,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> as well as a number of special reports on particular topics. These reports are prepared by teams of relevant researchers selected by the Bureau from government nominations. Drafts of these reports are made available for comment in open review processes to which anyone may contribute.</p>
<p>The IPCC published its <a href="/wiki/IPCC_First_Assessment_Report" title="IPCC First Assessment Report">first assessment report</a> in 1990, a supplementary report in 1992, a <a href="/wiki/IPCC_Second_Assessment_Report" title="IPCC Second Assessment Report">second assessment report (SAR)</a> in 1995, a <a href="/wiki/IPCC_Third_Assessment_Report" title="IPCC Third Assessment Report">third assessment report (TAR)</a> in 2001, a <a href="/wiki/IPCC_Fourth_Assessment_Report" title="IPCC Fourth Assessment Report">fourth assessment report (AR4)</a> in 2007 and a <a href="/wiki/IPCC_Fifth_Assessment_Report" title="IPCC Fifth Assessment Report">fifth assessment report (AR5)</a> in 2014.</p>
<p>Each assessment report is in three volumes, corresponding to Working Groups I, II, and III. Unqualified, "the IPCC report" is often used to mean the Working Group I report, which covers the basic science of climate change.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scope_and_preparation_of_the_reports">Scope and preparation of the reports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Scope and preparation of the reports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The IPCC does not carry out research nor does it monitor climate related data. Lead authors of IPCC reports assess the available information about climate change based on published sources.<sup id="cite_ref-itgp_sources_for_ipcc_reports_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-itgp_sources_for_ipcc_reports-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> According to IPCC guidelines, authors should give priority to peer-reviewed sources.<sup id="cite_ref-itgp_sources_for_ipcc_reports_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-itgp_sources_for_ipcc_reports-25">[25]</a></sup> Authors may refer to non-peer-reviewed sources (the "grey literature"), provided that they are of sufficient quality.<sup id="cite_ref-itgp_sources_for_ipcc_reports_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-itgp_sources_for_ipcc_reports-25">[25]</a></sup> Examples of non-peer-reviewed sources include model results, reports from government agencies and non-governmental organizations, and industry journals.<sup id="cite_ref-iac_sources_for_ipcc_report_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iac_sources_for_ipcc_report-7">[7]</a></sup> Each subsequent IPCC report notes areas where the science has improved since the previous report and also notes areas where further research is required.</p>
<p>There are generally three stages in the review process:<sup id="cite_ref-ipcc.ch_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ipcc.ch-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Expert review (6–8 weeks)</li>
<li>Government/expert review</li>
<li>Government review of:
<ul>
<li>Summaries for Policymakers</li>
<li>Overview Chapters</li>
<li>Synthesis Report</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Review comments are in an open archive for at least five years.</p>
<p>There are several types of endorsement which documents receive:</p>
<ul>
<li>Approval. Material has been subjected to detailed, line by line discussion and agreement.
<ul>
<li>Working Group Summaries for Policymakers are <i>approved</i> by their Working Groups.</li>
<li>Synthesis Report Summary for Policymakers is <i>approved</i> by Panel.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Adoption. Endorsed section by section (and not line by line).
<ul>
<li>Panel <i>adopts</i> Overview Chapters of Methodology Reports.</li>
<li>Panel <i>adopts</i> IPCC Synthesis Report.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Acceptance. Not been subject to line by line discussion and agreement, but presents a comprehensive, objective, and balanced view of the subject matter.
<ul>
<li>Working Groups <i>accept</i> their reports.</li>
<li>Task Force Reports are <i>accepted</i> by the Panel.</li>
<li>Working Group Summaries for Policymakers are <i>accepted</i> by the Panel after group <i>approval</i>.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The Panel is responsible for the IPCC and its endorsement of Reports allows it to ensure they meet IPCC standards.</p>
<p>There have been a range of commentaries on the IPCC's procedures, examples of which are discussed later in the article (see also <a href="/wiki/IPCC_Summary_for_Policymakers" title="IPCC Summary for Policymakers">IPCC Summary for Policymakers</a>). Some of these comments have been supportive,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> while others have been critical.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Some commentators have suggested changes to the IPCC's procedures.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Authors">Authors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Authors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(June 2016)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Each chapter has a number of authors who are responsible for writing and editing the material. A chapter typically has two "coordinating lead authors", ten to fifteen "lead authors", and a somewhat larger number of "contributing authors". The coordinating lead authors are responsible for assembling the contributions of the other authors, ensuring that they meet stylistic and formatting requirements, and reporting to the Working Group chairs. Lead authors are responsible for writing sections of chapters. Contributing authors prepare text, graphs or data for inclusion by the lead authors.</p>
<p>Authors for the IPCC reports are chosen from a list of researchers prepared by governments and participating organisations, and by the Working Group/Task Force Bureaux, as well as other experts known through their published work. The choice of authors aims for a range of views, expertise and geographical representation, ensuring representation of experts from developing and developed countries and countries with economies in transition.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_assessment_report">First assessment report</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: First assessment report">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/IPCC_First_Assessment_Report" title="IPCC First Assessment Report">IPCC First Assessment Report</a></div>
<p>The IPCC first assessment report was completed in 1990, and served as the basis of the UNFCCC.</p>
<p>The executive summary of the WG I Summary for Policymakers report says they are certain that emissions resulting from human activities are substantially increasing the atmospheric concentrations of the <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gases</a>, resulting on average in an additional warming of the <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a>'s surface. They calculate with confidence that CO<sub>2</sub> has been responsible for over half the enhanced greenhouse effect. They predict that under a "business as usual" (BAU) scenario, global mean temperature will increase by about 0.3&#160;°C per decade during the [21st] century. They judge that global mean surface air temperature has increased by 0.3 to 0.6&#160;°C over the last 100 years, broadly consistent with prediction of climate models, but also of the same magnitude as natural climate variability. The unequivocal detection of the enhanced greenhouse effect is not likely for a decade or more.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Supplementary_report_of_1992">Supplementary report of 1992</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Supplementary report of 1992">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 1992 supplementary report was an update, requested in the context of the negotiations on the UNFCCC at the <a href="/wiki/Earth_Summit" title="Earth Summit">Earth Summit</a> (United Nations Conference on Environment and Development) in <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a> in 1992.</p>
<p>The major conclusion was that research since 1990 did "not affect our fundamental understanding of the science of the greenhouse effect and either confirm or do not justify alteration of the major conclusions of the first IPCC scientific assessment". It noted that transient (time-dependent) simulations, which had been very preliminary in the FAR, were now improved, but did not include aerosol or ozone changes.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_assessment_report">Second assessment report</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Second assessment report">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/IPCC_Second_Assessment_Report" title="IPCC Second Assessment Report">IPCC Second Assessment Report</a></div>
<p><i>Climate Change 1995</i>, the IPCC Second Assessment Report (SAR), was finished in 1996. It is split into four parts:</p>
<ul>
<li>A synthesis to help interpret UNFCCC article 2.</li>
<li><i>The Science of Climate Change</i> (WG I)</li>
<li><i>Impacts, Adaptations and Mitigation of Climate Change</i> (WG II)</li>
<li><i>Economic and Social Dimensions of Climate Change</i> (WG III)</li>
</ul>
<p>Each of the last three parts was completed by a separate working group, and each has a Summary for Policymakers (SPM) that represents a consensus of national representatives. The SPM of the WG I report contains headings:</p>
<ol>
<li>Greenhouse gas concentrations have continued to increase</li>
<li>Anthropogenic <a href="/wiki/Aerosol" title="Aerosol">aerosols</a> tend to produce negative radiative forcings</li>
<li>Climate has changed over the past century (air temperature has increased by between 0.3 and 0.6&#160;°C since the late 19th century; this estimate has not significantly changed since the 1990 report).</li>
<li>The balance of evidence suggests a discernible human influence on global climate (considerable progress since the 1990 report in distinguishing between natural and anthropogenic influences on climate, because of: including aerosols; coupled models; pattern-based studies)</li>
<li>Climate is expected to continue to change in the future (increasing realism of simulations increases confidence; important uncertainties remain but are taken into account in the range of model projections)</li>
<li>There are still many uncertainties (estimates of future emissions and biogeochemical cycling; models; instrument data for model testing, assessment of variability, and detection studies)</li>
</ol>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Third_assessment_report">Third assessment report</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Third assessment report">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/IPCC_Third_Assessment_Report" title="IPCC Third Assessment Report">IPCC Third Assessment Report</a></div>
<p>The Third Assessment Report (TAR) was completed in 2001 and consists of four reports, three of them from its working groups:</p>
<ul>
<li>Working Group I: The Scientific Basis<sup id="cite_ref-IPCC_WG1_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPCC_WG1-31">[31]</a></sup></li>
<li>Working Group II: Impacts, Adaptation and Vulnerability<sup id="cite_ref-IPCC_WG2_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPCC_WG2-32">[32]</a></sup></li>
<li>Working Group III: Mitigation<sup id="cite_ref-IPCC_WG3_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPCC_WG3-33">[33]</a></sup></li>
<li>Synthesis Report<sup id="cite_ref-IPCC_Synth_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPCC_Synth-34">[34]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>A number of the TAR's conclusions are given quantitative estimates of how probable it is that they are correct, e.g., greater than 66% probability of being correct.<sup id="cite_ref-tar_uncertainties_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tar_uncertainties-35">[35]</a></sup> These are "<a href="/wiki/Bayesian_probability" title="Bayesian probability">Bayesian</a>" probabilities, which are based on an expert assessment of all the available evidence.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Robust findings" of the TAR Synthesis Report include:</p>
<ul>
<li>"Observations show Earth's surface is warming. Globally, 1990s very likely warmest decade in <a href="/wiki/Instrumental_temperature_record" title="Instrumental temperature record">instrumental record</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-tar_spm_robust_findings_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tar_spm_robust_findings-38">[38]</a></sup> Atmospheric concentrations of anthropogenic (i.e., human-emitted) <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gases</a> have increased substantially.<sup id="cite_ref-tar_spm_robust_findings_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tar_spm_robust_findings-38">[38]</a></sup></li>
<li>Since the mid-20th century, most of the observed warming is "likely" (greater than 66% probability, based on expert judgement)<sup id="cite_ref-tar_uncertainties_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tar_uncertainties-35">[35]</a></sup> due to human activities.<sup id="cite_ref-tar_spm_robust_findings_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tar_spm_robust_findings-38">[38]</a></sup></li>
<li>Projections based on the <i><a href="/wiki/Special_Report_on_Emissions_Scenarios" title="Special Report on Emissions Scenarios">Special Report on Emissions Scenarios</a></i> suggest warming over the 21st century at a more rapid rate than that experienced for at least the last 10,000 years.<sup id="cite_ref-tar_spm_robust_findings_38-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tar_spm_robust_findings-38">[38]</a></sup></li>
<li>"Projected climate change will have beneficial and adverse effects on both environmental and socio-economic systems, but the larger the changes and the rate of change in climate, the more the adverse effects predominate."<sup id="cite_ref-tar_spm_robust_findings_38-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tar_spm_robust_findings-38">[38]</a></sup></li>
<li>"<a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">Ecosystems</a> and <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a> are vulnerable to climate change and other stresses (as illustrated by observed impacts of recent regional temperature changes) and some will be irreversibly damaged or lost."<sup id="cite_ref-tar_spm_robust_findings_38-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tar_spm_robust_findings-38">[38]</a></sup></li>
<li>"Greenhouse gas emission reduction (<a href="/wiki/Climate_change_mitigation" title="Climate change mitigation">mitigation</a>) actions would lessen the pressures on natural and human systems from climate change."<sup id="cite_ref-tar_spm_robust_findings_38-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tar_spm_robust_findings-38">[38]</a></sup></li>
<li>"<a href="/wiki/Climate_change_adaptation" title="Climate change adaptation">Adaptation</a> [to the effects of climate change] has the potential to reduce adverse <a href="/wiki/Effects_of_global_warming" title="Effects of global warming">effects of climate change</a> and can often produce immediate ancillary benefits, but will not prevent all damages."<sup id="cite_ref-tar_spm_robust_findings_38-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tar_spm_robust_findings-38">[38]</a></sup> An example of adaptation to climate change is building <a href="/wiki/Levee" title="Levee">levees</a> in response to <a href="/wiki/Current_sea_level_rise" class="mw-redirect" title="Current sea level rise">sea level rise</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Comments_on_the_TAR">Comments on the TAR</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Comments on the TAR">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2001, 16 national <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_sciences" title="Academy of sciences">science academies</a> issued a joint statement on climate change.<sup id="cite_ref-2001_science_academies_statement_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2001_science_academies_statement-40">[40]</a></sup> The joint statement was made by the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Academy_of_Science" title="Australian Academy of Science">Australian Academy of Science</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Flemish_Academy_of_Belgium_for_Science_and_the_Arts" title="Royal Flemish Academy of Belgium for Science and the Arts">Royal Flemish Academy of Belgium for Science and the Arts</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Brazilian Academy of Sciences">Brazilian Academy of Sciences</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society_of_Canada" title="Royal Society of Canada">Royal Society of Canada</a>, the Caribbean Academy of Sciences, the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Chinese Academy of Sciences">Chinese Academy of Sciences</a>, the <a href="/wiki/French_Academy_of_Sciences" title="French Academy of Sciences">French Academy of Sciences</a>, the <a href="/wiki/German_Academy_of_Sciences_Leopoldina" class="mw-redirect" title="German Academy of Sciences Leopoldina">German Academy of Natural Scientists Leopoldina</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Science_Academy" title="Indian National Science Academy">Indian National Science Academy</a>, the Indonesian Academy of Sciences, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Irish_Academy" title="Royal Irish Academy">Royal Irish Academy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Accademia_dei_Lincei" title="Accademia dei Lincei">Accademia Nazionale dei Lincei</a> (Italy), the Academy of Sciences Malaysia, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society_of_New_Zealand" title="Royal Society of New Zealand">Academy Council of the Royal Society of New Zealand</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Swedish_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Royal Swedish Academy of Sciences">Royal Swedish Academy of Sciences</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society" title="Royal Society">Royal Society</a> (UK).<sup id="cite_ref-2001_science_academies_statement_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2001_science_academies_statement-40">[40]</a></sup> The statement, also published as an editorial in the journal <a href="/wiki/Science_(journal)" title="Science (journal)">Science</a>, stated "we support the [TAR's] conclusion that it is at least 90% certain that temperatures will continue to rise, with average global surface temperature projected to increase by between 1.4 and 5.8&#160;°C above 1990 levels by 2100".<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> The TAR has also been endorsed by the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Foundation_for_Climate_and_Atmospheric_Sciences" title="Canadian Foundation for Climate and Atmospheric Sciences">Canadian Foundation for Climate and Atmospheric Sciences</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-cfcas_tar_endorsement_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfcas_tar_endorsement-42">[42]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Meteorological_and_Oceanographic_Society" title="Canadian Meteorological and Oceanographic Society">Canadian Meteorological and Oceanographic Society</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-cmos_tar_endorsement_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cmos_tar_endorsement-43">[43]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/European_Geosciences_Union" title="European Geosciences Union">European Geosciences Union</a><sup id="cite_ref-egu_tar_endorsement_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-egu_tar_endorsement-44">[44]</a></sup> (refer to "<a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change#Endorsements_of_the_IPCC" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">Endorsements of the IPCC</a>").</p>
<p>In 2001, the <a href="/wiki/US_National_Research_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="US National Research Council">US National Research Council</a> (US NRC)<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> produced a report that assessed Working Group I's (WGI) contribution to the TAR. US NRC (2001)<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> "generally agrees" with the WGI assessment, and describes the full WGI report as an "admirable summary of research activities in climate science".<sup id="cite_ref-nap.edu_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nap.edu-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>IPCC author <a href="/wiki/Richard_Lindzen" title="Richard Lindzen">Richard Lindzen</a> has made a number of criticisms of the TAR.<sup id="cite_ref-lindzen_tar_critique_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lindzen_tar_critique-48">[48]</a></sup> Among his criticisms, Lindzen has stated that the WGI Summary for Policymakers (SPM) does not faithfully summarize the full WGI report.<sup id="cite_ref-lindzen_tar_critique_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lindzen_tar_critique-48">[48]</a></sup> For example, Lindzen states that the SPM understates the uncertainty associated with <a href="/wiki/Global_climate_model" class="mw-redirect" title="Global climate model">climate models</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-lindzen_tar_critique_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lindzen_tar_critique-48">[48]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_T._Houghton" title="John T. Houghton">John Houghton</a>, who was a co-chair of TAR WGI,<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> has responded to Lindzen's criticisms of the SPM.<sup id="cite_ref-houghton_lindzen_rebuttal_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-houghton_lindzen_rebuttal-50">[50]</a></sup> Houghton has stressed that the SPM is agreed upon by delegates from many of the world's governments, and that any changes to the SPM must be supported by scientific evidence.<sup id="cite_ref-houghton_lindzen_rebuttal_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-houghton_lindzen_rebuttal-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>IPCC author <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Trenberth" class="mw-redirect" title="Kevin Trenberth">Kevin Trenberth</a> has also commented on the WGI SPM.<sup id="cite_ref-trenberth_tar_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trenberth_tar-51">[51]</a></sup> Trenberth has stated that during the drafting of the WGI SPM, some government delegations attempted to "blunt, and perhaps obfuscate, the messages in the report".<sup id="cite_ref-trenberth_tar_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trenberth_tar-51">[51]</a></sup> However, Trenberth concludes that the SPM is a "reasonably balanced summary".<sup id="cite_ref-trenberth_tar_51-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trenberth_tar-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>US NRC (2001)<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> concluded that the WGI SPM and Technical Summary are "consistent" with the full WGI report. US NRC (2001)<sup id="cite_ref-nap.edu_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nap.edu-47">[47]</a></sup> stated:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>[...] the full [WGI] report is adequately summarized in the Technical Summary. The full WGI report and its Technical Summary are not specifically directed at policy. The Summary for Policymakers reflects less emphasis on communicating the basis for uncertainty and a stronger emphasis on areas of major concern associated with human-induced climate change. This change in emphasis appears to be the result of a summary process in which scientists work with policy makers on the document. Written responses from U.S. coordinating and lead scientific authors to the committee indicate, however, that (a) no changes were made without the consent of the convening lead authors (this group represents a fraction of the lead and contributing authors) and (b) most changes that did occur lacked significant impact.</p>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fourth_assessment_report">Fourth assessment report</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Fourth assessment report">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/IPCC_Fourth_Assessment_Report" title="IPCC Fourth Assessment Report">IPCC Fourth Assessment Report</a></div>
<p>The Fourth Assessment Report (AR4) was published in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-ar4_press_flyer_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar4_press_flyer-53">[53]</a></sup> Like previous assessment reports, it consists of four reports:</p>
<ul>
<li>Working Group I: The Physical Science Basis</li>
<li>Working Group II: Impacts, Adaptation and Vulnerability</li>
<li>Working Group III: Mitigation</li>
<li>Synthesis Report</li>
</ul>
<p>People from over 130 countries contributed to the IPCC Fourth Assessment Report, which took 6 years to produce.<sup id="cite_ref-ar4_press_flyer_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar4_press_flyer-53">[53]</a></sup> Contributors to AR4 included more than 2500 scientific expert reviewers, more than 800 contributing authors, and more than 450 lead authors.<sup id="cite_ref-ar4_press_flyer_53-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar4_press_flyer-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Robust findings" of the Synthesis report include:<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>"Warming of the climate system is unequivocal, as is now evident from observations of increases in global average air and ocean temperatures, widespread melting of snow and ice and rising global average sea level".<sup id="cite_ref-ar4_main_observations_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar4_main_observations-55">[55]</a></sup></li>
<li>Most of the global average warming over the past 50 years is "very likely" (greater than 90% probability, based on expert judgement)<sup id="cite_ref-ar4_uncertainty_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar4_uncertainty-56">[56]</a></sup> due to human activities.<sup id="cite_ref-ar4_main_observations_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar4_main_observations-55">[55]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>"Impacts [of climate change] will very likely increase due to increased frequencies and intensities of some extreme weather events".<sup id="cite_ref-ar4_projected_impacts_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar4_projected_impacts-57">[57]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li>"Anthropogenic warming and sea level rise would continue for centuries even if GHG emissions were to be reduced sufficiently for GHG concentrations to stabilise, due to the time scales associated with climate processes and feedbacks".<sup id="cite_ref-ar4_projected_impacts_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar4_projected_impacts-57">[57]</a></sup> Stabilization of atmospheric greenhouse gas concentrations is discussed in <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_mitigation" title="Climate change mitigation">climate change mitigation</a>.</li>
<li>"Some planned adaptation (of human activities) is occurring now; more extensive adaptation is required to reduce vulnerability to climate change".<sup id="cite_ref-ar4_policy_responses_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar4_policy_responses-58">[58]</a></sup></li>
<li>"Unmitigated climate change would, in the long term, be likely to exceed the capacity of natural, managed and human systems to adapt".<sup id="cite_ref-ar4_policy_responses_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar4_policy_responses-58">[58]</a></sup></li>
<li>"Many impacts [of climate change] can be reduced, delayed or avoided by mitigation".<sup id="cite_ref-ar4_policy_responses_58-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar4_policy_responses-58">[58]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>Global warming projections from AR4<sup id="cite_ref-ar4_spm_projections_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar4_spm_projections-59">[59]</a></sup> are shown below. The projections apply to the end of the 21st century (2090–99), relative to temperatures at the end of the 20th century (1980–99). Add 0.7&#160;°C to projections to make them relative to pre-industrial levels instead of 1980–99.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Descriptions of the greenhouse gas emissions scenarios can be found in <a href="/wiki/Special_Report_on_Emissions_Scenarios" title="Special Report on Emissions Scenarios">Special Report on Emissions Scenarios</a>.</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<td>1.4 – 3.8</td>

<td>2.0 – 5.4</td>

</tr>
</table>
<p>"Likely" means greater than 66% probability of being correct, based on expert judgement.<sup id="cite_ref-ar4_uncertainty_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar4_uncertainty-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Response_to_AR4">Response to AR4</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Response to AR4">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Several <a href="/wiki/Science_academy" class="mw-redirect" title="Science academy">science academies</a> have referred to and/or reiterated some of the conclusions of AR4. These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Joint-statements made in 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-2007_science_academies_statement_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2007_science_academies_statement-61">[61]</a></sup> 2008<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> and 2009<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> by the science academies of Brazil, China, India, Mexico, South Africa and the <a href="/wiki/G8" class="mw-redirect" title="G8">G8</a> nations (the "G8+5").</li>
<li>Publications by the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Academy_of_Science" title="Australian Academy of Science">Australian Academy of Science</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></li>
<li>A joint-statement made in 2007 by the <a href="/wiki/Network_of_African_Science_Academies" title="Network of African Science Academies">Network of African Science Academies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></li>
<li>A statement made in 2010 by the Inter Academy Medical Panel<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> This statement has been signed by 43 scientific academies.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[a]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Environmental_Assessment_Agency" title="Netherlands Environmental Assessment Agency">Netherlands Environmental Assessment Agency</a> (PBL, <i>et al.</i>, 2009;<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> 2010)<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> has carried out two reviews of AR4. These reviews are generally supportive of AR4's conclusions.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pbl_2010_ipcc_review_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbl_2010_ipcc_review-71">[70]</a></sup> PBL (2010)<sup id="cite_ref-pbl_2010_ipcc_review_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbl_2010_ipcc_review-71">[70]</a></sup> make some recommendations to improve the IPCC process. A literature assessment by the US National Research Council (US NRC, 2010)<sup id="cite_ref-us_nrc_2010_summary_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-us_nrc_2010_summary-72">[71]</a></sup> concludes:</p>
<blockquote>
<p><b>Climate change is occurring, is caused largely by human activities, and poses significant risks for—and in many cases is already affecting—a broad range of human and natural systems</b> [<i>emphasis in original text</i>]. [...] This conclusion is based on a substantial array of scientific evidence, including recent work, and is consistent with the conclusions of recent assessments by the U.S. Global Change Research Program [...], the Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change’s Fourth Assessment Report [...], and other assessments of the state of scientific knowledge on climate change.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Some errors have been found in the IPCC AR4 Working Group II report. Two errors include the melting of <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayan</a> <a href="/wiki/Glacier" title="Glacier">glaciers</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change#Projected_date_of_melting_of_Himalayan_glaciers" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">later section</a>), and Dutch land area that is below sea level.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fifth_assessment_report">Fifth assessment report</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Fifth assessment report">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/IPCC_Fifth_Assessment_Report" title="IPCC Fifth Assessment Report">IPCC Fifth Assessment Report</a></div>
<p>The IPCC's Fifth Assessment Report (AR5) was completed in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-ar5_leaflet_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar5_leaflet-74">[73]</a></sup> AR5 followed the same general format as of AR4, with three Working Group reports and a Synthesis report.<sup id="cite_ref-ar5_leaflet_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar5_leaflet-74">[73]</a></sup> The Working Group I report (WG1) was published in September 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-ar5_leaflet_74-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ar5_leaflet-74">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>Conclusions of AR5 are summarized below:</p>
<dl>
<dt>Working Group I</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>"Warming of the climate system is unequivocal, and since the 1950s, many of the observed changes are unprecedented over decades to millennia".<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup></li>
<li>"Atmospheric concentrations of carbon dioxide, methane, and nitrous oxide have increased to levels unprecedented in at least the last 800,000 years".<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup></li>
<li>Human influence on the climate system is clear.<sup id="cite_ref-IPCC_AR5_attribution_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPCC_AR5_attribution-77">[76]</a></sup> It is extremely likely (95-100% probability)<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup> that human influence was the dominant cause of global warming between 1951-2010.<sup id="cite_ref-IPCC_AR5_attribution_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IPCC_AR5_attribution-77">[76]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dt>Working Group II</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>"Increasing magnitudes of [global] warming increase the likelihood of severe, pervasive, and irreversible impacts"<sup id="cite_ref-Summary_for_Policymakers_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Summary_for_Policymakers-79">[78]</a></sup></li>
<li>"A first step towards adaptation to future climate change is reducing vulnerability and exposure to present climate variability"<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup></li>
<li>"The overall risks of climate change impacts can be reduced by limiting the rate and magnitude of climate change"<sup id="cite_ref-Summary_for_Policymakers_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Summary_for_Policymakers-79">[78]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dt>Working Group III</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>Without new policies to mitigate climate change, projections suggest an increase in global mean temperature in 2100 of <a href="/wiki/4_Degrees_and_Beyond_International_Climate_Conference" title="4 Degrees and Beyond International Climate Conference">3.7 to 4.8&#160;°C</a>, relative to pre-industrial levels (<a href="/wiki/Median" title="Median">median</a> values; the range is 2.5 to 7.8&#160;°C including climate uncertainty).<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup></li>
<li>The current trajectory of global greenhouse gas emissions is not consistent with limiting global warming to below 1.5 or 2&#160;°C, relative to pre-industrial levels.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> Pledges made as part of the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_Nations_Climate_Change_Conference" title="2010 United Nations Climate Change Conference">Cancún Agreements</a> are broadly consistent with cost-effective scenarios that give a "likely" chance (66-100% probability) of limiting global warming (in 2100) to below 3&#160;°C, relative to pre-industrial levels.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Representative_Concentration_Pathways">Representative Concentration Pathways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Representative Concentration Pathways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Projections in AR5 are based on "<a href="/wiki/Representative_Concentration_Pathways" title="Representative Concentration Pathways">Representative Concentration Pathways</a>" (RCPs).<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> The RCPs are consistent with a wide range of possible changes in future anthropogenic greenhouse gas emissions. Projected changes in global mean surface temperature and sea level are given in the main <a href="/wiki/Representative_Concentration_Pathways" title="Representative Concentration Pathways">RCP article</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_reports">Special reports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Special reports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In addition to climate assessment reports, the IPCC is publishing Special Reports on specific topics. The preparation and approval process for all IPCC Special Reports follows the same procedures as for IPCC Assessment Reports. In the year 2011 two IPCC Special Report were finalized, the Special Report on <a href="/wiki/Renewable_Energy_Sources_and_Climate_Change_Mitigation" title="Renewable Energy Sources and Climate Change Mitigation">Renewable Energy Sources and Climate Change Mitigation</a> (SRREN) and the Special Report on Managing Risks of Extreme Events and Disasters to Advance Climate Change Adaptation (SREX). Both Special Reports were requested by governments.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-85">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_Report_on_Emissions_Scenarios_.28SRES.29">Special Report on Emissions Scenarios (SRES)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Special Report on Emissions Scenarios (SRES)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Special_Report_on_Emissions_Scenarios" title="Special Report on Emissions Scenarios">Special Report on Emissions Scenarios</a> (SRES) is a report by the IPCC which was published in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> The SRES contains "<a href="/wiki/Climate_change_scenario" title="Climate change scenario">scenarios</a>" of future changes in emissions of greenhouse gases and <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">sulfur dioxide</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> One of the uses of the SRES scenarios is to project future changes in climate, e.g., changes in global mean temperature. The SRES scenarios were used in the IPCC's Third<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> and Fourth Assessment Reports.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>The SRES scenarios are "baseline" (or "reference") scenarios, which means that they do not take into account any current or future measures to limit greenhouse gas (GHG) emissions (e.g., the <a href="/wiki/Kyoto_Protocol" title="Kyoto Protocol">Kyoto Protocol</a> to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Framework_Convention_on_Climate_Change" title="United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change">United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> SRES emissions projections are broadly comparable in range to the baseline projections that have been developed by the scientific community.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Comments_on_the_SRES">Comments on the SRES</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Comments on the SRES">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>There have been a number of comments on the SRES. Parson <i>et al.</i> (2007)<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> stated that the SRES represented "a substantial advance from prior scenarios". At the same time, there have been criticisms of the SRES.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>The most prominently publicized criticism of SRES focused on the fact that all but one of the participating models compared gross domestic product (GDP) across regions using <a href="/wiki/Market_exchange_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Market exchange rate">market exchange rates</a> (MER), instead of the more correct <a href="/wiki/Purchasing-power_parity" class="mw-redirect" title="Purchasing-power parity">purchasing-power parity</a> (PPP) approach.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> This criticism is discussed in the <a href="/wiki/Special_Report_on_Emissions_Scenarios#MER_and_PPP" title="Special Report on Emissions Scenarios">main SRES article</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_report_on_renewable_energy_sources_and_climate_change_mitigation_.28SRREN.29">Special report on renewable energy sources and climate change mitigation (SRREN)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Special report on renewable energy sources and climate change mitigation (SRREN)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://srren.ipcc-wg3.de/">report</a> assesses existing literature on <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_commercialisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Renewable energy commercialisation">renewable energy commercialisation</a> for the mitigation of climate change. It covers the six most important renewable energy technologies, as well as their integration into present and future energy systems. It also takes into consideration the environmental and social consequences associated with these technologies, the cost and strategies to overcome technical as well as non-technical obstacles to their application and diffusion.</p>
<p>More than 130 authors from all over the world contributed to the preparation of IPCC Special Report on Renewable Energy Sources and Climate Change Mitigation (SRREN) on a voluntary basis – not to mention more than 100 scientists, who served as contributing authors.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-85">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_Report_on_managing_the_risks_of_extreme_events_and_disasters_to_advance_climate_change_adaptation_.28SREX.29">Special Report on managing the risks of extreme events and disasters to advance climate change adaptation (SREX)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Special Report on managing the risks of extreme events and disasters to advance climate change adaptation (SREX)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://ipcc-wg2.gov/SREX/">report</a> assesses the effect that climate change has on the threat of natural disasters and how nations can better manage an expected change in the frequency of occurrence and intensity of severe weather patterns. It aims to become a resource for decision-makers to prepare more effectively for managing the risks of these events. A potentially important area for consideration is also the detection of trends in extreme events and the attribution of these trends to human influence.</p>
<p>More than 80 authors, 19 review editors, and more than 100 contributing authors from all over the world contributed to the preparation of SREX.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_85-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-85">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Methodology_reports">Methodology reports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Methodology reports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Within IPCC the National Greenhouse Gas Inventory Program develops methodologies to estimate emissions of <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gases</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> This has been undertaken since 1991 by the IPCC WGI in close collaboration with the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Energy_Agency" title="International Energy Agency">International Energy Agency</a>. The objectives of the National Greenhouse Gas Inventory Program are:</p>
<ul>
<li>to develop and refine an internationally agreed methodology and software for the calculation and reporting of national greenhouse gas emissions and removals; and</li>
<li>to encourage the widespread use of this methodology by countries participating in the IPCC and by signatories of the UNFCCC.</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Revised_1996_IPCC_Guidelines_for_National_Greenhouse_Gas_Inventories">Revised 1996 IPCC Guidelines for National Greenhouse Gas Inventories</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Revised 1996 IPCC Guidelines for National Greenhouse Gas Inventories">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The 1996 Guidelines for National Greenhouse Gas Investories provide the methodological basis for the estimation of national greenhouse gas <a href="/wiki/Emission_inventory" title="Emission inventory">emissions inventories</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> Over time these guidelines have been completed with good practice reports: <i>Good Practice Guidance and Uncertainty Management in National Greenhouse Gas Inventories</i> and <i>Good Practice Guidance for Land Use, Land-Use Change and Forestry</i>.</p>
<p>The 1996 guidelines and the two good practice reports are to be used by parties to the UNFCCC and to the <a href="/wiki/Kyoto_Protocol" title="Kyoto Protocol">Kyoto Protocol</a> in their annual submissions of national greenhouse gas inventories.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2006_IPCC_Guidelines_for_National_Greenhouse_Gas_Inventories">2006 IPCC Guidelines for National Greenhouse Gas Inventories</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: 2006 IPCC Guidelines for National Greenhouse Gas Inventories">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The 2006 <i>IPCC Guidelines for National Greenhouse Gas Inventories</i> is the latest version of these emission estimation methodologies, including a large number of default emission factors.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (December 2011)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> Although the IPCC prepared this new version of the guidelines on request of the parties to the UNFCCC, the methods have not yet been officially accepted for use in national greenhouse gas emissions reporting under the UNFCCC and the Kyoto Protocol.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Activities">Activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The IPCC concentrates its activities on the tasks allotted to it by the relevant WMO Executive Council and UNEP Governing Council resolutions and decisions as well as on actions in support of the UNFCCC process.<sup id="cite_ref-principles_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-principles-6">[6]</a></sup> While the preparation of the assessment reports is a major IPCC function, it also supports other activities, such as the Data Distribution Centre<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> and the National Greenhouse Gas Inventories Programme,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup> required under the UNFCCC. This involves publishing default <a href="/wiki/Emission_factor" class="mw-redirect" title="Emission factor">emission factors</a>, which are factors used to derive emissions estimates based on the levels of fuel consumption, industrial production and so on.</p>
<p>The IPCC also often answers inquiries from the UNFCCC Subsidiary Body for Scientific and Technological Advice (SBSTA).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Nobel_Peace_Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Nobel Peace Prize">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2007_Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="2007 Nobel Peace Prize">2007 Nobel Peace Prize</a></div>
<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wikisource-logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/38px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png" width="38" height="40" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/57px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/76px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="410" data-file-height="430" /></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist"><a href="/wiki/Wikisource" title="Wikisource">Wikisource</a> has original text related to this article:
<div style="margin-left: 10px;"><b><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Al_Gore%27s_Nobel_Peace_Prize_acceptance_speech" class="extiw" title="wikisource:Al Gore's Nobel Peace Prize acceptance speech">Al Gore's Nobel Peace Prize acceptance speech</a></b></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In December 2007, the IPCC was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> "for their efforts to build up and disseminate greater knowledge about man-made climate change, and to lay the foundations for the measures that are needed to counteract such change". The award is shared with Former U.S. Vice-President <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a> for his work on climate change and the documentary <i><a href="/wiki/An_Inconvenient_Truth" title="An Inconvenient Truth">An Inconvenient Truth</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-nobelpeaceprize_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nobelpeaceprize-103">[102]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticisms">Criticisms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Criticisms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There is <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change#Endorsements_of_the_IPCC" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">widespread support</a> for the IPCC in the <a href="/wiki/Scientific_community" title="Scientific community">scientific community</a>, which is reflected in publications by other scientific bodies<sup id="cite_ref-2001_science_academies_statement_40-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2001_science_academies_statement-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2007_science_academies_statement_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2007_science_academies_statement-61">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-us_nrc_2010_summary_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-us_nrc_2010_summary-72">[71]</a></sup> and experts.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> However, criticisms of the IPCC have been made.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since 2010 the IPCC has come under yet unparalleled public and political scrutiny.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> The global <a href="/w/index.php?title=IPCC_consensus&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="IPCC consensus (page does not exist)">IPCC consensus</a> approach has been challenged internally<sup id="cite_ref-ess_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ess-107">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MO_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MO-108">[107]</a></sup> and externally with the 2009 <a href="/wiki/Climatic_Research_Unit_email_controversy" title="Climatic Research Unit email controversy">Climatic Research Unit email controversy</a> ("Climategate") an important (but not sole) threshold.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> It has been deemed an <a href="/wiki/Natural_monopoly" title="Natural monopoly">information monopoly</a> with results for both the quality and the impact of the IPCC work as such.<sup id="cite_ref-ess_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ess-107">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tol2010_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tol2010-110">[109]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Projected_date_of_melting_of_Himalayan_glaciers">Projected date of melting of Himalayan glaciers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Projected date of melting of Himalayan glaciers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_the_IPCC_AR4" class="mw-redirect" title="Criticism of the IPCC AR4">Criticism of the IPCC AR4</a></div>
<p>A paragraph in the 2007 Working Group II report ("Impacts, Adaptation and Vulnerability"), chapter 10 included a projection that Himalayan glaciers could disappear by 2035</p>
<dl>
<dd><i>Glaciers in the Himalaya are receding faster than in any other part of the world (see Table 10.9) and, if the present rate continues, the likelihood of them disappearing by the year 2035 and perhaps sooner is very high if the Earth keeps warming at the current rate. Its total area will likely shrink from the present 500,000 to 100,000 km<sup>2</sup> by the year 2035 (WWF, 2005).</i></dd>
</dl>
<p>This projection was not included in the final summary for policymakers. The IPCC has since acknowledged that the date is incorrect, while reaffirming that the conclusion in the final summary was robust. They expressed regret for "the poor application of well-established IPCC procedures in this instance". The date of 2035 has been correctly quoted by the IPCC from the WWF report, which has misquoted its own source, an <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Commission_on_Snow_and_Ice_Hydrology&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="International Commission on Snow and Ice Hydrology (page does not exist)">ICSI</a> report "Variations of Snow and Ice in the past and at present on a Global and Regional Scale".</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Rajendra_K._Pachauri" title="Rajendra K. Pachauri">Rajendra K. Pachauri</a> responded in an interview with <i>Science</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Watson_criticism">Watson criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Watson criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Former IPCC chairman <a href="/wiki/Robert_Watson_(scientist)" title="Robert Watson (scientist)">Robert Watson</a> has said "The mistakes all appear to have gone in the direction of making it seem like climate change is more serious by overstating the impact. That is worrying. The IPCC needs to look at this trend in the errors and ask why it happened".<sup id="cite_ref-Times_Online_2010-02-15_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Times_Online_2010-02-15-112">[111]</a></sup> Martin Parry, a climate expert<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> who had been co-chair of the IPCC working group II, said that "What began with a single unfortunate error over Himalayan glaciers has become a clamour without substance" and the IPCC had investigated the other alleged mistakes, which were "generally unfounded and also marginal to the assessment".<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_2010-02-14_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian_2010-02-14-114">[113]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emphasis_of_the_.22hockey_stick.22_graph">Emphasis of the "hockey stick" graph</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Emphasis of the &quot;hockey stick&quot; graph">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Hockey_stick_graph" title="Hockey stick graph">Hockey stick graph</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hockey_stick_controversy" title="Hockey stick controversy">Hockey stick controversy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:T_comp_61-90.pdf" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/T_comp_61-90.pdf/page1-300px-T_comp_61-90.pdf.jpg" width="300" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/T_comp_61-90.pdf/page1-450px-T_comp_61-90.pdf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/T_comp_61-90.pdf/page1-600px-T_comp_61-90.pdf.jpg 2x" data-file-width="875" data-file-height="660" /></a>
